## Tier RBAC — Permission-Based Access Control *(low priority)*

> **Design intent**: Implement a granular, permission-based access control system layered on top of the existing role system. This enables hiring interns/employees (e.g. content moderator, finance manager, ad manager, SEO manager, blog poster, event handler, review manager, site manager) who each get a tailored subset of admin panel access — without ever granting them the full `admin` role. All permission checks are SSR-enforced (Server Components + API route guards) so users cannot manipulate their own access via browser devtools.
>
> **Core model**: `admin` role = full access (bypasses all checks). New `employee` role = access determined entirely by `permissions: Permission[]` field on their `UserDocument`. Roles are bundles of permissions at setup time; each individual employee can have custom overrides on top of their preset group.
>
> **Permission naming convention**: `admin:resource:action` (e.g. `admin:blog:publish`, `admin:payouts:write`, `admin:events:delete`).
>
> **Enforcement layers (in order)**:
> 1. `proxy.ts` middleware — role gate: is user `admin` or `employee`? If neither, redirect to `/unauthorized` before any page renders.
> 2. `src/app/[locale]/admin/layout.tsx` (RSC) — fetches `permissions[]` from Firestore server-side; checks `admin:dashboard:view`; redirects if absent.
> 3. Section-level `layout.tsx` files (RSC) — each admin route group gets its own layout that checks the section-specific permission (e.g. `/admin/blog/layout.tsx` checks `admin:blog:read`).
> 4. API routes — `requirePermission(request, permission)` wrapper applied to every admin API endpoint; admin role bypasses.
> 5. Firestore security rules — users cannot write their own `permissions`, `role`, or `permissionGroup` fields; only Admin SDK (server) can.
>
> **Employee preset groups (16 bundles — assigned at invite time, customisable per-user)**:
>
> | Group | Typical intern role | Permissions granted |
> |---|---|---|
> | `content_moderator` | Content intern | `admin:dashboard:view`, `admin:reviews:read/write/delete`, `admin:products:read`, `admin:users:read`, `admin:blog:read` |
> | `review_manager` | Review intern | `admin:dashboard:view`, `admin:reviews:read/write/delete`, `admin:products:read`, `admin:users:read` |
> | `blog_poster` | Blog writer | `admin:dashboard:view`, `admin:blog:read/write` (NOT delete, NOT publish), `admin:media:read/write` |
> | `community_manager` | Social/community | `admin:dashboard:view`, `admin:events:read/write/delete`, `admin:event-entries:read/write`, `admin:blog:read/write/publish`, `admin:reviews:read`, `admin:notifications:read/write`, `admin:newsletter:read/write`, `admin:media:read/write` |
> | `event_handler` | Events intern | `admin:dashboard:view`, `admin:events:read/write/delete`, `admin:event-entries:read/write`, `admin:notifications:read/write` |
> | `newsletter_manager` | Email marketing | `admin:dashboard:view`, `admin:newsletter:read/write`, `admin:contact:read`, `admin:users:read` |
> | `seo_manager` | SEO intern | `admin:dashboard:view`, `admin:faqs:read/write/delete`, `admin:blog:read/write/publish`, `admin:navigation:read/write`, `admin:sections:read/write`, `admin:site:read` |
> | `ad_manager` | Ads intern | `admin:dashboard:view`, `admin:ads:read/write/delete`, `admin:carousel:read/write/delete`, `admin:deals:read/write`, `admin:featured:read/write`, `admin:sections:read/write` |
> | `site_manager` | Site/CMS manager | `admin:dashboard:view`, `admin:site:read/write`, `admin:navigation:read/write`, `admin:sections:read/write`, `admin:carousel:read/write`, `admin:faqs:read/write`, `admin:media:read/write` |
> | `catalog_manager` | Catalog intern | `admin:dashboard:view`, `admin:categories:read/write/delete`, `admin:brands:read/write/delete`, `admin:products:read/write`, `admin:media:read/write`, `admin:deals:read/write`, `admin:featured:read/write` |
> | `finance_manager` | Finance intern | `admin:dashboard:view`, `admin:analytics:view`, `admin:payouts:read/write`, `admin:orders:read`, `admin:returns:read` |
> | `data_analyst` | Analytics (read-only) | `admin:dashboard:view`, `admin:analytics:view`, `admin:orders:read`, `admin:payouts:read`, `admin:products:read`, `admin:users:read`, `admin:reviews:read`, `admin:carts:read`, `admin:wishlists:read`, `admin:bids:read` |
> | `customer_support` | Support agent | `admin:dashboard:view`, `admin:orders:read/write`, `admin:returns:read/write`, `admin:users:read`, `admin:contact:read`, `admin:notifications:read/write` |
> | `store_onboarding` | Seller success | `admin:dashboard:view`, `admin:stores:read/write`, `admin:store-addresses:read`, `admin:users:read`, `admin:notifications:write` |
> | `trust_and_safety` | Trust & safety | `admin:dashboard:view`, `admin:users:read/write`, `admin:orders:read`, `admin:products:read/write`, `admin:reviews:read/write/delete`, `admin:bids:read/write`, `admin:sessions:read/delete`, `admin:carts:read` |
> | `auction_monitor` | Auction intern | `admin:dashboard:view`, `admin:bids:read/write`, `admin:products:read`, `admin:orders:read`, `admin:users:read`, `admin:notifications:write` |
> | `scam_moderator` | Scam/trust intern | `admin:dashboard:view`, `admin:scammers:read/write/verify/delete`, `admin:users:read`, `admin:media:read/write` |
> | `support_agent` | Customer support | `admin:dashboard:view`, `admin:support-tickets:read/write/assign/close`, `admin:orders:read/write`, `admin:returns:read/write`, `admin:users:read`, `admin:contact:read`, `admin:notifications:read/write` |
>
> **Store capabilities (per-store flags)**: stored as `capabilities?: StoreCapability[]` on `StoreDocument`. Managed by admin via `AdminStoreEditorView`. Checked server-side on every relevant store API route — client visibility is UX only, not security. Available capabilities split into two tiers:
>
> **Listing & Catalog capabilities** (control what types of listings a store can create):
>
> | Capability | Default | What it unlocks |
> |---|---|---|
> | `host_auctions` | ✗ | Can create auction listings (`/store/auctions`). Not all stores are trusted to run auctions — requires admin approval. |
> | `host_preorders` | ✗ | Can create pre-order listings (`/store/pre-orders`). Indicates store has a supplier relationship. |
> | `create_categories` | ✗ | Can request new category creation from the storefront (goes to admin for approval). Power sellers only. |
> | `suggest_brands` | ✓ | Can suggest new brands via form (admin reviews before publishing). On by default for all stores. |
> | `create_coupons` | ✓ | Can create store-level coupons (`/store/coupons`). On by default. |
> | `bulk_listing_import` | ✗ | Can bulk-import products via CSV template. Requires admin setup of import schema per store. |
> | `extended_return_window` | ✗ | Store can offer 30-day returns (platform default is 7 days). Contractual agreement required. |
>
> **Trust & Visibility capabilities** (control how a store appears on the platform):
>
> | Capability | Default | What it unlocks |
> |---|---|---|
> | `verified_seller` | ✗ | Shows "Verified" badge on store profile + product cards. Admin manually grants after identity verification. |
> | `featured_placement` | ✗ | Store is eligible to appear in featured stores sections and homepage store rows. |
> | `promotional_banner` | ✗ | Store's banner can be used in homepage carousel / promotional sections by admin. |
> | `priority_support` | ✗ | Store queries go to a dedicated support queue with faster SLA. |
>
> **Platform & Technical capabilities** (control platform-level privileges):
>
> | Capability | Default | What it unlocks |
> |---|---|---|
> | `multiple_stores` | ✗ | Owner can create more than one store (default: 1 per user). Admin grants per seller agreement. |
> | `custom_store_slug` | ✗ | Can change their store URL slug after initial setup (default: locked after first 7 days). |
> | `api_access` | ✗ | Store gets API credentials for programmatic product/order access (future: for power sellers with integrations). |
> | `lower_commission_rate` | ✗ | Negotiated reduced platform commission. Requires a `customCommissionRate: number` field on `StoreDocument` alongside this capability. |
> | `early_access_features` | ✗ | Store sees beta features before GA (e.g. new listing types, new analytics views). |
> | `advanced_analytics` | ✗ | Access to detailed analytics (cohort retention, basket analysis, top-buyer breakdown). Standard stores get summary only. |
>
> **Do RBAC1 → RBAC3 → RBAC10 → RBAC5 → RBAC4 → RBAC7 → RBAC6 → RBAC8 → RBAC9 in order** (each task depends on the previous).

| # | Task | Complexity | Status | Notes |
|---|------|-----------|--------|-------|
| RBAC1 | Permission constants + UserDocument schema extension | S | ⏳ | **New file** `appkit/src/features/auth/permissions/constants.ts`: (1) `Permission` union type — all ~85 permission strings: core admin (`admin:dashboard:view`, `admin:users:read/write/delete`, `admin:products:read/write/delete`, `admin:orders:read/write`, `admin:returns:read/write`, `admin:stores:read/write`, `admin:store-addresses:read`, `admin:analytics:view`, `admin:payouts:read/write`, `admin:categories:read/write/delete`, `admin:brands:read/write/delete`, `admin:coupons:read/write/delete`, `admin:deals:read/write`, `admin:featured:read/write`, `admin:reviews:read/write/delete`, `admin:blog:read/write/delete/publish`, `admin:bids:read/write`, `admin:media:read/write/delete`, `admin:site:read/write`, `admin:navigation:read/write`, `admin:sections:read/write`, `admin:carousel:read/write/delete`, `admin:ads:read/write/delete`, `admin:faqs:read/write/delete`, `admin:newsletter:read/write`, `admin:contact:read`, `admin:events:read/write/delete`, `admin:event-entries:read/write`, `admin:sessions:read/delete`, `admin:notifications:read/write`, `admin:carts:read`, `admin:wishlists:read`, `admin:feature-flags:read/write`, `admin:copilot:view`, `admin:team:read/write`); **moderation** (`admin:user-bans:read`, `admin:user-bans:write`, `admin:support-tickets:read`, `admin:support-tickets:write`, `admin:support-tickets:assign`, `admin:support-tickets:close`); **scam** (`admin:scammers:read`, `admin:scammers:write`, `admin:scammers:verify`, `admin:scammers:delete`). (2) `EmployeeGroup` union (18 presets + custom): `"content_moderator" \| "review_manager" \| "blog_poster" \| "community_manager" \| "event_handler" \| "newsletter_manager" \| "seo_manager" \| "ad_manager" \| "site_manager" \| "catalog_manager" \| "finance_manager" \| "data_analyst" \| "customer_support" \| "store_onboarding" \| "trust_and_safety" \| "auction_monitor" \| "scam_moderator" \| "support_agent" \| "custom"`. (3) `PERMISSION_GROUPS: Record<EmployeeGroup, Permission[]>` — all 18 preset bundles per the table above. (4) `ROUTE_PERMISSION_MAP: Record<string, Permission>` — maps each `/admin/[section]` path to its required read permission. (5) `StoreCapability` union (18 capabilities across 3 tiers). **Schema extension** in `appkit/src/features/auth/schemas/firestore.ts`: add `"employee"` to `UserRole` union; add `permissions?: Permission[]` and `permissionGroup?: EmployeeGroup` to `UserDocument`; add `capabilities?: StoreCapability[]` and `customCommissionRate?: number` to `StoreDocument`. Export all new types from `appkit/src/features/auth/client.ts` and `server.ts`. `npx tsc --noEmit` → 0 errors in both repos. |
| RBAC2 | Server-side permission resolver | M | ⏳ | Depends on RBAC1. **New file** `appkit/src/features/auth/server/getServerPermissions.ts`: (1) `getServerPermissions(uid: string): Promise<Permission[]>` — fetches user doc from Firestore Admin SDK; if `role === "admin"` returns a sentinel `ALL_PERMISSIONS` constant (all permissions granted); if `role === "employee"` returns `user.permissions ?? []`; for any other role returns `[]`. (2) `hasPermission(permissions: Permission[], required: Permission): boolean` — pure check; if `permissions === ALL_PERMISSIONS` always returns true. (3) `hasAnyPermission(permissions: Permission[], required: Permission[]): boolean`. (4) `requirePermission(request: NextRequest, permission: Permission): Promise<UserDocument>` — wraps `requireAuthFromRequest` + `getServerPermissions`; throws `NextResponse.json({ error: "Forbidden" }, { status: 403 })` if permission absent; admin bypasses. Export from `appkit` server barrel. |
| RBAC3 | Admin layout SSR permission gate | M | ⏳ | Depends on RBAC2. Convert `src/app/[locale]/admin/layout.tsx` from client `<ProtectedRoute requireRole="admin">` to a **Server Component**: (1) call `getServerSessionUser()` — if null, `redirect(ROUTES.AUTH.LOGIN)`; (2) if `user.role !== "admin" && user.role !== "employee"`, `redirect("/unauthorized")`; (3) call `getServerPermissions(user.uid)` — if does not include `admin:dashboard:view`, `redirect("/unauthorized")`; (4) pass `{ user, permissions }` as props to a new `AdminLayoutShell` client component (the existing sidebar/layout UI stays client-side). The shell component shows only nav items the employee has permission to see (RBAC7 wires this). Keep existing visual layout identical — only auth logic changes. Ensure the shell receives `permissions` as a serialisable prop (string array). `npx tsc --noEmit` → 0 errors. |
| RBAC4 | Section-level SSR permission layouts | L | ⏳ | Depends on RBAC3. Add a `layout.tsx` (Server Component) for each admin section group. Each layout: (1) calls `getServerSessionUser()` + `getServerPermissions(uid)`; (2) checks the section's read permission; (3) if user is `admin`, renders children immediately (no check); (4) if `employee` without the permission, renders `<UnauthorizedPage />` (new component: centred lock icon + "You don't have access to this section. Contact your admin." + Back button). Create one layout file per section: `admin/blog/layout.tsx` (checks `admin:blog:read`), `admin/reviews/layout.tsx` (`admin:reviews:read`), `admin/events/layout.tsx` + `admin/event-entries/layout.tsx` (`admin:events:read`), `admin/analytics/layout.tsx` (`admin:analytics:view`), `admin/payouts/layout.tsx` (`admin:payouts:read`), `admin/categories/layout.tsx` (`admin:categories:read`), `admin/brands/layout.tsx` (`admin:brands:read`), `admin/coupons/layout.tsx` (`admin:coupons:read`), `admin/deals/layout.tsx` (`admin:deals:read`), `admin/featured/layout.tsx` (`admin:featured:read`), `admin/bids/layout.tsx` (`admin:bids:read`), `admin/media/layout.tsx` (`admin:media:read`), `admin/site/layout.tsx` (`admin:site:read`), `admin/navigation/layout.tsx` (`admin:navigation:read`), `admin/sections/layout.tsx` (`admin:sections:read`), `admin/carousel/layout.tsx` (`admin:carousel:read`), `admin/ads/layout.tsx` (`admin:ads:read`), `admin/faqs/layout.tsx` (`admin:faqs:read`), `admin/newsletter/layout.tsx` (`admin:newsletter:read`), `admin/contact/layout.tsx` (`admin:contact:read`), `admin/users/layout.tsx` (`admin:users:read`), `admin/products/layout.tsx` (`admin:products:read`), `admin/orders/layout.tsx` (`admin:orders:read`), `admin/return-requests/layout.tsx` (`admin:returns:read`), `admin/stores/layout.tsx` (`admin:stores:read`), `admin/store-addresses/layout.tsx` (`admin:store-addresses:read`). **System sections** (`sessions`, `notifications`, `carts`, `wishlists`, `feature-flags`, `copilot`, `team`) get `layout.tsx` files that also check their respective system permissions — these effectively lock out all employees unless explicitly granted (which the admin should rarely do). `npx tsc --noEmit` → 0 errors. |
| RBAC5 | API route permission guards | M | ⏳ | Depends on RBAC2. Apply `requirePermission(request, permission)` to every admin API route that currently uses `requireRoleFromRequest(request, ["admin"])`. Replace with the finer-grained permission check. **File-by-file**: every route under `src/app/api/admin/` gets the corresponding write permission on mutating methods (POST/PUT/PATCH/DELETE) and read permission on GET. Example: `src/app/api/admin/blog/route.ts` GET → `admin:blog:read`; POST → `admin:blog:write`; `admin/blog/[id]/route.ts` DELETE → `admin:blog:delete`. Routes not yet guarded (see RBAC research findings — only 2 of 35 route families had any guard) must all get guards in this task. Admin always passes (requirePermission bypasses for `role === "admin"`). No change to store or user API routes in this task. `npx tsc --noEmit` → 0 errors. |
| RBAC6 | Admin Team management page | L | ⏳ | Depends on RBAC1, RBAC5. **New page** `/admin/team` — manages employee accounts. (1) **`AdminTeamView`** (`appkit/src/features/admin/components/AdminTeamView.tsx`): lists all users with `role === "employee"`. Filter chip row: All / by group (16 presets). Row actions: Edit permissions (SideDrawer), Revoke access (ConfirmDeleteModal → sets `isDisabled: true` + clears `permissions`). "Invite Employee" button top-right. On save: `PUT /api/admin/team/[id]` writes `{ role: "employee", permissions, permissionGroup }` via Admin SDK. (3) **API routes**: `GET /api/admin/team` (list employees — filters `role=employee` from users collection), `POST /api/admin/team` (invite — creates Firebase Auth user with temp password + sets role=employee + initial permissions from group + sends invite email via SendGrid), `PUT /api/admin/team/[id]` (update permissions + group), `DELETE /api/admin/team/[id]` (revoke — sets isDisabled=true, does NOT delete the Firestore user doc so audit trail is preserved). | RBAC8 | Store capabilities system | M | ⏳ | Depends on RBAC1. (1) **Schema**: `StoreCapability` union and `capabilities?: StoreCapability[]` + `customCommissionRate?: number` are added to `StoreDocument` in RBAC1. (5) **Admin UI**: expand `AdminStoreEditorView` SideDrawer (VA12) — add "Capabilities" section with three collapsible sub-groups matching the three capability tiers (Listing & Catalog / Trust & Visibility / Platform & Technical); use `Checkbox` per capability with a short description label. Grayed-out + tooltip for `lower_commission_rate` unless a `customCommissionRate` numeric field is filled in first. Save via existing PUT `/api/admin/stores/[id]`. (6) **Store dashboard UI**: capability-gated features show a locked UI with "Not available for your store — contact support" rather than crashing or 404ing. Client visibility check reads capabilities from the store context (fetched once on store layout mount). Server always re-checks. (7) **Seed data**: update `stores-seed-data.ts` — `letitrip-official` gets all capabilities (full featured flagship store); `pokemon-palace`, `cardgame-hub`, `beyblade-arena` get `["suggest_brands","create_coupons","host_auctions","verified_seller","featured_placement"]`; `diecast-depot`, `tokyo-toys-india` get `["suggest_brands","create_coupons","host_auctions","host_preorders","verified_seller"]`; `gundam-galaxy`, `vintage-vault` get `["suggest_brands","create_coupons","host_preorders","verified_seller"]`. `npx tsc --noEmit` → 0 errors. |
| RBAC9 | Firestore security rules — block permission self-escalation | S | ⏳ | Depends on RBAC1. Update `appkit/firebase/base/firestore.rules` (the base file that feeds into the root `firestore.rules` via `firebase-merge.mjs`). Add rules to the `/users/{userId}` match block: (1) Disallow any authenticated user from writing `role`, `permissions`, or `permissionGroup` fields on their own document — these fields can only be written by the Admin SDK (which bypasses Firestore rules entirely via service account). Implementation: `allow write: if false` on a rule that triggers when `request.resource.data.diff(resource.data).affectedKeys().hasAny(["role", "permissions", "permissionGroup"])` — unless the requesting user is a verified admin (check `request.auth.token.admin == true` from custom claims). (2) Add custom claim `admin: true` to the Admin SDK token via `setCustomUserClaims(uid, { admin: true })` in a Cloud Function triggered on user role change — this ensures Firestore rules can distinguish Admin SDK writes from client writes. After: run `firebase emulators:start` and verify a client write to `permissions` field is rejected with `PERMISSION_DENIED`. Run `firebase-merge.mjs` before deploying. |
| RBAC10 | Proxy.ts middleware first gate | S | ⏳ | Depends on RBAC1. Extend `src/proxy.ts` (Next.js 16 middleware file) to add a cheap first gate for `/admin/*` routes: (1) Extract session cookie (`__session`) — verify via Firebase Admin SDK `verifySessionCookie()` (already available in middleware context). (2) Read `role` from the decoded token or from a minimal Firestore read (use a cached read — `getServerSessionUser()` equivalent). (3) If role is not `"admin"` and not `"employee"`: immediately return `NextResponse.redirect(new URL("/unauthorized", request.url))` — do NOT let the page render at all. (4) If role is `"admin"`: allow through without any further check (full access). (5) If role is `"employee"`: allow through — the RSC layout (RBAC3) will do the fine-grained permission check with a Firestore read. **Important**: do NOT do a full Firestore permission read in middleware — it runs on Edge and Firestore Admin SDK may not be available there. Keep the middleware check role-only; the full permission enforcement happens in the Server Component layouts. Also add `/unauthorized` to the public route allowlist (never redirect the unauthorized page itself). |

---

## Tier BAN — User Moderation & Trust *(low priority)*

> **Design intent**: Give LetItRip admins fine-grained control over user behaviour without needing the nuclear option of a full account ban for every infraction. A soft ban restricts specific actions (writing reviews, joining events, placing bids, etc.) while letting the user continue browsing. A hard ban disables the Firebase Auth account entirely and cascades to suspend listings, cancel active bids, and revoke sessions. The support ticket system is built here because it is the primary channel through which bans get contested and resolved.
>
> **Soft ban model**: `UserDocument.softBans: UserSoftBan[]` — an array of scoped restrictions. Each entry has `action: BannedAction`, `reason: string`, `bannedBy: string` (employee uid), `bannedAt: Date`, `expiresAt?: Date` (null = permanent). Supported `BannedAction` values: `write_reviews`, `write_blog_comments`, `join_events`, `place_bids`, `create_listings`, `send_messages`, `create_support_tickets`, `report_scammers`. A user may have multiple simultaneous soft bans of different types.
>
> **Hard ban model**: `isDisabled: true` (already on `UserDocument`) + `hardBanReason?: string` + `hardBannedAt?: Date` + `hardBannedBy?: string`. Triggers Firebase Auth `updateUser(uid, { disabled: true })` via Admin SDK.
>
> **Support ticket rules** (enforced server-side, no client trust):
> - Max **2 active** (status: `open` | `in_progress` | `waiting_on_user`) general tickets per user at any time.
> - Order tickets: exactly **1 per non-completed order** (orders in status `PENDING`, `PROCESSING`, `SHIPPED`, `RETURN_REQUESTED` only — not `DELIVERED`, `CANCELLED`, `REFUNDED`).
> - Guests cannot create tickets — authentication required.
> - If user has `create_support_tickets` soft ban → 403 "Your account is restricted from opening support tickets."
> - New ticket in same category not allowed while an existing one in that category is in `waiting_on_user` status (prevents spam reopening).
>
> **Notification routing (Firebase Functions)**: ticket events → notify user + notify all employees who have `admin:support-tickets:read` permission. Ban events → notify user + notify all employees with `admin:user-bans:read` permission. Notifications written to the `notifications` Firestore collection (existing schema) + Firebase Cloud Messaging push if device token present.
>
> **Do BAN1 → BAN2 → BAN3 → BAN4 → BAN5 → BAN6 → BAN7 → BAN8 → BAN9 in order.**

| # | Task | Complexity | Status | Notes |
|---|------|-----------|--------|-------|
| BAN1 | Schema — ban fields on UserDocument + SupportTicket collection | S | ⏳ | **(1) UserDocument additions** in `appkit/src/features/auth/schemas/firestore.ts`: `softBans?: UserSoftBan[]`; `hardBanReason?: string`; `hardBannedAt?: Timestamp`; `hardBannedBy?: string`. **New types** `BannedAction = "write_reviews" \| "write_blog_comments" \| "join_events" \| "place_bids" \| "create_listings" \| "send_messages" \| "create_support_tickets" \| "report_scammers"` and `UserSoftBan = { action: BannedAction; reason: string; bannedBy: string; bannedAt: Timestamp; expiresAt?: Timestamp \| null }`. **(2) New collection** `supportTickets` — new file `appkit/src/features/support/schemas/firestore.ts`. `SupportTicketDocument`: `id` (prefix `ticket-`, auto-ID), `userId: string`, `userEmail: string` (denormalized), `userDisplayName: string`, `category: TicketCategory`, `subject: string`, `description: string`, `orderId?: string` (linked when category=`order_issue`), `status: TicketStatus`, `priority: "low" \| "normal" \| "high" \| "urgent"`, `assignedTo?: string` (employee uid), `assignedToName?: string`, `internalNotes?: string` (admin-only, never sent to user), `messages: TicketMessage[]`, `resolvedAt?: Timestamp`, `closedAt?: Timestamp`, `createdAt: Timestamp`, `updatedAt: Timestamp`. **`TicketCategory`**: `"order_issue" \| "billing_payment" \| "account" \| "listing_dispute" \| "scam_report" \| "refund_request" \| "auction_dispute" \| "general"`. **`TicketStatus`**: `"open" \| "in_progress" \| "waiting_on_user" \| "resolved" \| "closed"`. **`TicketMessage`**: `{ id: string; authorId: string; authorRole: "user" \| "support" \| "admin"; body: string; attachments?: string[]; createdAt: Timestamp }`. Add `SupportRepository` stub (`appkit/src/repositories/support.repository.ts`) with methods: `createTicket`, `getUserTickets(userId)`, `getTicketById`, `countActiveTickets(userId)`, `getActiveOrderTicket(userId, orderId)`, `updateTicketStatus`, `addMessage`, `assignTicket`. Export from appkit. `npx tsc --noEmit` → 0 errors. |
| BAN2 | Soft ban enforcement — server-side action guards | M | ⏳ | Depends on BAN1. Create `appkit/src/features/auth/server/checkSoftBan.ts`: `isSoftBanned(user: UserDocument, action: BannedAction): boolean` — checks `user.softBans[]`; ignores entries where `expiresAt` is in the past (expired bans are treated as lifted without deletion). **Wire enforcement into API routes**: (1) `POST /api/reviews` → check `write_reviews`; (2) `POST /api/blog/[id]/comments` (future) → check `write_blog_comments`; (3) `POST /api/events/[id]/entries` → check `join_events`; (4) `POST /api/bids` → check `place_bids`; (5) `POST /api/store/products` (and auction/preorder) → check `create_listings` (on the seller's user doc); (6) `POST /api/support/tickets` → check `create_support_tickets`; (7) `POST /api/scammers/report` → check `report_scammers`. Each check: call `requireAuthFromRequest`, fetch user doc, call `isSoftBanned` — if true, return `403 { error: "Your account is restricted from [action]. Reason: [reason]. Contact support if you believe this is an error." }`. Admin and employee role bypass soft ban checks. **Also**: write `getBanSummary(user): { activeBans: UserSoftBan[], expiredBans: UserSoftBan[] }` helper for display in user settings and admin view. `npx tsc --noEmit` → 0 errors. |
| BAN3 | Hard ban enforcement + cascade | M | ⏳ | Depends on BAN1. **Apply hard ban** via new API route `POST /api/admin/users/[id]/hard-ban` (requires `admin:user-bans:write`): (1) Call Firebase Admin `auth.updateUser(uid, { disabled: true })` to block login; (2) Set `isDisabled: true`, `hardBanReason`, `hardBannedAt`, `hardBannedBy` on UserDocument; (3) Cascade: delete all `sessions/{id}` docs where `userId === uid` (revoke active sessions); (4) If user is a seller: set store `status: "suspended"` and bulk-set all their product/auction/preorder `status: "archived"`; (5) Cancel all `bids` where `bidderId === uid` and `status: "active"` → set to `"cancelled"`; (6) Write a `notifications` doc to user: "Your account has been permanently suspended. [reason]. You may appeal by emailing support@letitrip.in." **Lift hard ban** via `POST /api/admin/users/[id]/unban`: calls `auth.updateUser(uid, { disabled: false })`; clears `isDisabled/hardBanReason/hardBannedAt/hardBannedBy`; does NOT auto-restore listings — admin manually re-activates those via products page. **Soft ban apply/lift**: `POST /api/admin/users/[id]/soft-ban` (action, reason, expiresAt?); `DELETE /api/admin/users/[id]/soft-ban/[action]`. Notification on apply: "Your account has been restricted from [action]. Reason: [reason]. Expires: [date or 'Never']." `npx tsc --noEmit` → 0 errors. |
| BAN4 | Support ticket API + limit enforcement engine | M | ⏳ | Depends on BAN1. **`POST /api/support/tickets`** (authenticated only — no guests): (1) Verify auth (no guest tokens accepted); (2) Check `create_support_tickets` soft ban; (3) Load ticket limits from `siteSettings.platformLimits.maxOpenTicketsPerUser` (default 2) and `siteSettings.platformLimits.maxOrderTicketsPerOrder` (default 1); (4) For `category !== "order_issue"`: call `supportRepository.countActiveTickets(userId)` — if ≥ 2 return `422 { error: "You already have 2 open tickets. Please wait for them to be resolved before opening a new one." }`; (5) For `category === "order_issue"`: validate `orderId` is present; fetch order — reject if order `status` is `DELIVERED`, `CANCELLED`, or `REFUNDED` (`400 { error: "Support tickets can only be opened for active orders." }`); call `supportRepository.getActiveOrderTicket(userId, orderId)` — if exists return `422 { error: "You already have an open ticket for this order." }`; (6) Check same-category duplication: if an active ticket with the same category and `status: "waiting_on_user"` exists, reject `422 { error: "You have an unanswered question from support for this topic. Please respond to your existing ticket first." }`; (7) Create ticket doc with `status: "open"`, `priority: "normal"`. **`GET /api/support/tickets`** (user's own tickets, paginated). **`POST /api/support/tickets/[id]/messages`** (add message to thread — both user and assigned support can use this). **`GET/PATCH /api/admin/support-tickets`** (admin list + status/assignment update, requires `admin:support-tickets:read/write`). All validation server-side, never trusted from client. `npx tsc --noEmit` → 0 errors. |

| BAN7 | Admin support ticket management page | L | ⏳ | Depends on BAN4. **New admin section** `/admin/support-tickets` (add to `ADMIN_NAV_GROUPS` Management group, guarded by `admin:support-tickets:read`). **(1) `AdminSupportTicketsView`** (`appkit/src/features/admin/components/`): list all tickets. | BAN9 | Firebase Functions — ticket lifecycle + ban notifications | M | ⏳ | Depends on BAN1, BAN4. New functions in `functions/src/triggers/`: **(1) `onSupportTicketCreate`** (Firestore `onCreate` on `supportTickets/{ticketId}`): write a `notifications` doc for the ticket author (`type: "ticket_opened"`, `title: "Support ticket received"`, `body: "We've received your ticket: [subject]. Our team will respond within 24–48 hours."`); query all users with `role === "employee"` and `permissions` containing `admin:support-tickets:read`, write a `notifications` doc for each (`type: "new_support_ticket"`, `title: "New ticket: [subject]"`, `body: "From [userDisplayName] · Category: [category] · Priority: normal"`). **(2) `onSupportTicketUpdate`** (Firestore `onUpdate`): detect `status` field change; if changed → write notification to ticket author with new status description (e.g. "Your ticket is now in progress. An agent has been assigned."; "Your ticket has been resolved. Reply if you need further help."); if `assignedTo` changed → write notification to new assignee (`type: "ticket_assigned"`, `body: "Ticket '[subject]' has been assigned to you."`); if priority changed to `urgent` → additionally notify all employees with `admin:support-tickets:read`. **(3) `onUserBanApplied`** (Firestore `onUpdate` on `users/{uid}` — detect `softBans` array growth or `isDisabled` flipping to true): write notification to banned user explaining the restriction + reason; write notification to all employees with `admin:user-bans:read` (`type: "user_banned"`, `body: "[displayName] has been [hard/soft] banned by [actorName]. Reason: [reason]."`). **(4) `onUserUnbanned`** (detect `isDisabled` flipping to false): write notification to restored user ("Your account access has been restored."); notify `admin:user-bans:read` employees. All functions use the existing `notifications` collection shape. Use `Promise.all` for batch notification writes. `npx tsc --noEmit` → 0 errors in `functions/`. |

---

## Tier SCAM — Scam Awareness System *(low priority)*

> **Design intent**: A publicly visible, SEO-optimised scam database that (1) educates the collectibles community about how they get cheated, (2) names known bad actors with evidence, and (3) is mandatory reading for all new registrants. Admin employees verify and publish scammer profiles. The system is deeply integrated with the RBAC tier — only `scam_moderator` and `trust_and_safety` employees can verify profiles; any authenticated user can submit a report.
>
> **27 scam types** across 6 categories (defined as `SCAM_TYPES` constant in `appkit/src/features/scams/constants/scam-types.ts`):
>
> | Category | Types |
> |---|---|
> | **Price Manipulation** | `undervaluation` — tricks seller into believing item is worth far less ("it's just an old toy"); `fake_price_reference` — fake screenshot showing lower price elsewhere; `bait_and_switch` — advertises one price, changes after engagement; `condition_misrepresentation` — lists mint/sealed/graded, ships damaged/fake |
> | **Social Engineering** | `sympathy_play` — impersonates a student/child who "can't afford" market price, guilt-trips seller into discount or deferred payment; `trust_building_fraud` — months of small friendly purchases then one large scam; `urgency_pressure` — "I'm leaving the city in 1 hour, send now"; `student_impersonation` — specific variant: claims to be a broke student collector |
> | **Payment Fraud** | `advance_payment_ghost` — takes full advance payment then ghosts; `fake_payment_screenshot` — sends photoshopped UPI/PayTM success screenshot; `partial_payment_ghost` — pays earnest money, takes delivery, ghosts for rest; `chargeback_fraud` — pays via Razorpay/credit card, receives item, disputes with bank; `overpayment_scam` — "accidentally" overpays ₹5,000 for ₹500 item, asks for ₹4,500 refund before initial payment clears |
> | **Pre-order & Delivery Fraud** | `preorder_hold` — collects deposits from many buyers, holds money for months claiming "delays", eventually refunds only after public noise — never had a supplier; `fake_preorder_listing` — lists high-demand limited items for preorder with zero supplier relationship; `endless_delay_scam` — ships deliberately late (after refund window closes) with vague updates |
> | **Identity & Impersonation** | `seller_impersonation` — steals product photos from a reputable seller and runs identical listing at slightly lower price; `platform_impersonation` — fake "LetItRip Support" WhatsApp/DM asking for OTP/bank details; `account_takeover_resale` — hacks/takes over dormant legitimate seller account to exploit their review history; `fake_escrow` — creates a fake "middleman escrow" that is themselves |
> | **Item Authenticity Fraud** | `counterfeit_item` — sells replica/bootleg as genuine (fake holographic Pokémon cards, recast Funko Pops, reproduction vintage Hot Wheels); `fake_grading_claim` — claims PSA/BGS graded, shows photoshopped certificate; `graded_case_tampering` — cracks a legitimate PSA slab, swaps in a fake/lower card, reseals; `sealed_product_repack` — opens booster boxes, removes valuable pulls, reseals with hot glue, resells as factory sealed |
> | **Logistics Fraud** | `empty_box_ship` — ships an empty box or rocks/newspaper; `fake_tracking_number` — generates tracking label but never drops package at courier; `return_swap_fraud` — receives genuine item, returns empty box or damaged swap, claims refund |
>
> **Scammer profile document** (`scammers` Firestore collection, prefix `scammer-`): `id`, `slug`, `displayName` (as they presented themselves), `phones: string[]`, `upiIds: string[]`, `emails: string[]`, `socialMedia: { platform: SocialPlatform; handle: string; url?: string }[]`, `scamType: ScamType`, `scamPlatform: ScamPlatform`, `description: string` (rich HTML — detailed account of what happened), `amountLost?: number` (paise), `itemInvolved?: string`, `evidence: string[]` (media URLs — chat screenshots, payment screenshots, listing photos), `reportedBy: string` (userId), `reportedByAnon: boolean` (if reporter chose to remain anonymous in public view), `status: "pending_review" \| "verified" \| "rejected" \| "removed"`, `verifiedBy?: string`, `verifiedAt?: Timestamp`, `relatedScammerIds: string[]`, `tags: string[]`, `seoSlug: string`, `views: number`, `createdAt: Timestamp`, `updatedAt: Timestamp`. **`ScamPlatform`**: `"letitrip" \| "whatsapp" \| "olx" \| "facebook_marketplace" \| "instagram_dms" \| "telegram" \| "in_person" \| "local_market" \| "other"`. **`SocialPlatform`**: `"instagram" \| "facebook" \| "twitter_x" \| "whatsapp" \| "telegram" \| "youtube" \| "other"`.
>
> **SEO-first design**: every scammer profile page has a unique `/scams/[slug]` route, full `generateMetadata` (name in title, scam type in description, og:image from evidence), FAQ schema JSON-LD, and phone/UPI/email plaintext in the HTML so they are indexed by search engines. The goal: someone searching a phone number or UPI ID finds our page immediately.
>
> **Mandatory registration acknowledgement**: after email verification, new users see a non-skippable scam awareness modal with 5 key facts (one per scam category), a link to `/scams`, and a required checkbox "I have read the scam awareness guide and understand these risks." Tracked as `scamAwarenessAcknowledgedAt?: Timestamp` on `UserDocument`. The modal is shown until acknowledged; after acknowledgement it never appears again.
>
> **Do SCAM1 → SCAM2 → SCAM3 → SCAM4 → SCAM5 → SCAM6 → SCAM7 → SCAM8 in order. SCAM9 (RBAC wiring) should be done alongside RBAC4/RBAC7 when that tier is implemented.**

## Tier EX — Extended Homepage Sections

> **Design intent**: Enhancements to existing homepage section types. All changes are backward-compatible. Old section docs without new fields render using existing defaults. Admin builders in AdminSectionsView.tsx expose new config fields. Schema changes go in appkit/src/features/homepage/schemas/firestore.ts; live-stats.ts extended for collection queries. Do EX1 -> EX2 -> EX3 -> EX4 -> EX5 in order.
>
> **EX5 note**: the new collection-cards section type does NOT delete the 8 specialized section types — those remain as legacy aliases. Admin can create new sections using the unified type; old sections render via existing components until migrated.

## Tier AX — Action System & URL Patterns

> **Design intent**: (1) Eliminate ~200 copy-pasted onClick router.push + toast chains across admin/store/public pages via a typed ACTION constant system with useActionDispatch() hook. (2) Make every admin/store CRUD panel deep-linkable via URL search params (?panel=create / ?panel=edit&id=slug). (3) Standardise sticky form action bars across all FormShell-based forms.
>
> **Implementation order**: AX1 -> AX2 (depends on AX1) -> AX3 (depends on UX1 FormShell).

| # | Task | Complexity | Status | Notes |
|---|------|-----------|--------|-------|
| AX1 | Centralized ACTION constants + useActionDispatch hook | M | ✅ | **Session 90 (2026-05-11) — fully done.** Constants: `appkit/src/features/products/constants/action-defs.ts` — ACTION_ID/ROW_ACTION_ID/FORM_ACTION_ID/DASHBOARD_QUICK_ACTION_ID + all META maps + preset groups. Hook: `appkit/src/react/hooks/use-action-dispatch.ts` — useActionDispatch(options?) returns async dispatch(action) handling NAVIGATE/OPEN_PANEL/TOAST/BULK/COPY. Store: `appkit/src/stores/panel-store.ts` — Zustand usePanelStore (panelId, data, openPanel, closePanel, isPanelOpen). Zustand v5 added to appkit deps. Migration: SellerProductsView.tsx handleEdit migrated from router.push to dispatch({ type: "NAVIGATE" }). All exported from client.ts + index.ts. 0 TS errors both repos, appkit build clean. |
| AX2 | Edit/Create URL routing — panel auto-open on URL params | M | ✅ | **Session 92 (2026-05-11) — done.** usePanelUrlSync hook (URL ?panel=create/edit&id=xxx); DataTable onRowClick prop; embedded prop on all 7 AdminXxxEditorViews; 8 admin listing views wired with inline SideDrawer + embedded editor; exported from index.ts + client.ts. 0 TS errors both repos. | Depends on AX1. **Pattern**: listing pages read URL search params ?panel=create or ?panel=edit&id={slug}. On mount: if params present -> dispatch(ACTION.OPEN_PANEL(panelId, { id })). On panel onClose/onSuccess -> router.replace(basePath) (removes query params). **usePanelUrlSync(panelId, basePath)** hook (new, appkit/src/hooks/): reads useSearchParams(), on mount calls dispatch if params match, subscribes to panelStore — when panel closes, calls router.replace(basePath). **Deep-link format**: /admin/products?panel=create (create panel opens); /admin/products?panel=edit&id=product-abc (edit panel opens pre-loaded). **Wire into**: admin products, auctions, preorders, stores, categories, brands, blog, events, FAQs, coupons (10 admin listing pages) + all store-seller listing pages. **Share**: copy icon in panel header -> ACTION.COPY(window.location.href, "Edit link copied") after URL is updated on open. Add ROUTES.ADMIN.PRODUCT_EDIT(id) etc. helper functions to route-map. npx tsc --noEmit -> 0 errors. |
| AX3 | Sticky form action bars — desktop top + mobile bottom | S | ✅ | **Session 92 (2026-05-11) — done.** FormActionBar component (sticky top desktop, sticky bottom mobile, breadcrumbs, dirty-dot, Discard/Preview/Save Draft/Publish); isDirty flag; browser tab title "* " prefix; ConfirmModal on Esc when dirty; wired in FormShell. 0 TS errors both repos. | Depends on UX1 (FormShell). Extends FormShell spec: **Desktop** — sticky top bar: breadcrumb trail + resource name + [Preview] [Save Draft] [Publish]. Position: sticky top-[var(--header-height,0px)] z-[var(--appkit-z-dropdown)]. Background: var(--appkit-color-surface) with bottom border. **Mobile** (< md) — sticky bottom bar: [Discard] [Save Draft] [Publish]. Position: sticky bottom-0, same z-index. Top bar hidden on mobile (space constraint). **Dirty state**: when any form field changes, set isDirty flag. Browser tab title prepends "* " while dirty. Esc when dirty: show ConfirmModal ("Discard unsaved changes?") before closing. **Toast on action**: Save Draft -> toast "Draft saved" (success). Publish -> toast "Published successfully" (success). Validation error -> toast "Fix the errors above" (error) + scroll to first error field. **FormActionBar** component (new, appkit/src/ui/components/): props { title, breadcrumbs, onSaveDraft, onPublish, onPreview, onDiscard, isDirty, isSubmitting }. Used by FormShell. npx tsc --noEmit -> 0 errors. |
| A1-ext | Admin product create: store picker dropdown | S | ✅ | Already present pre-S1 | `AdminProductEditorView.tsx` already has a `DynamicSelect` store picker at the top of the form (lines 214-228), loading stores via `ADMIN_ENDPOINTS.STORES`. This view is admin-only by namespace so the field is already correctly scoped. Sellers use separate `SellerCreateProductView` / `SellerEditProductView` which auto-set storeId. No code change needed. |

## Tier FI — Product Feature Icons & Badges

> **Design intent**: A flexible feature-flagging system for listings. Platform defines standard icons (free shipping, verified seller, condition badges, etc.). Stores and admin can create custom feature icons. Products carry a features: string[] array of feature IDs. Cards and detail pages render small icon badges. Some features are product-type specific (e.g., Auction Winner Badge applies to auctions only). Slug prefix: feature-.

| # | Task | Complexity | Status | Notes |
|---|------|-----------|--------|-------|
| FI1 | productFeatures schema + repository | S | ⏳ | **New file** appkit/src/features/products/schemas/product-features.ts. ProductFeatureDocument: id (slug, prefix feature-), slug, label, description (optional), icon (icon name key from appkit icon set OR SVG path string), iconColor (optional CSS var token key e.g. "--appkit-color-primary"), category ("shipping"/"seller"/"condition"/"platform"/"auction"/"preorder"/"custom"), scope ("platform"/"store"), productTypes (array: "product"/"auction"/"preorder"/"all"), storeId (optional, required if scope=store), isActive (boolean), displayOrder (number), createdAt (Timestamp). Register slug prefix feature- in CLAUDE.md slug table. **Repository** appkit/src/repositories/product-features.repository.ts: list({ scope?, storeId?, productType?, isActive? }), findById(id), create(data), update(id, data), delete(id), listPlatform(), listForStore(storeId). **ProductDocument extension**: add features?: string[] (optional array of feature IDs — absent = no features) to appkit/src/features/products/schemas/firestore.ts. Export from appkit. npx tsc --noEmit -> 0 errors. |

## Tier BK — Public Bulk Actions

> **Design intent**: Let both authenticated and guest users select multiple products on listing pages and perform bulk actions (compare, wishlist, share). Selection state is ephemeral (in-memory only, not persisted). Guest users can compare and share; auth users additionally add to wishlist. Compare is capped at 4 items. The compare overlay shows items side-by-side (desktop: table; mobile: swipeable cards).

Wired on Products/Auctions/PreOrders/Stores listings. `isSelecting` derived from `selectedCount > 0` — no separate boolean state needed. `BaseListingCard` root updated to accept/forward long-press event props. **Session 85 quality pass**: `BulkActionsBar` `actions` array now requires a stable `key` field (replaces array-index key); `danger` variant uses `var(--appkit-color-danger)` CSS token; `Button` import for clear action. `ListingToolbar` now accepts `labels?: ListingToolbarLabels` prop for i18n overrides; VIEW_BTN_* class constants extracted. `MarketplaceAuctionCard` countdown status colours extracted to `COUNTDOWN_STATUS_CLASS` module-level const with dark mode variants. |

## Tier WA — WhatsApp Business Integration *(low priority — post-alpha)*

> **Design intent**: Allow store owners to sync their standard products to their own WhatsApp Business Catalog (per-store Meta credentials). Platform admin receives a WhatsApp message (Meta Cloud API) whenever a new order is placed — announcement also sent to the store owner. Group posting is not possible via API; a wa.me share link is provided instead. Full plan in `C:\Users\mohsi\.claude\plans\plan-and-add-support-compressed-snowflake.md`.

State: `waPhoneNumberId`, `waCloudApiToken` (MaskedInput), `waAdminNotifyNumbers` (plain Input, hint: comma-sep digits w/ country code). Populate from `s.credentialsMasked` in existing useEffect. | WA8 | Route constant + store nav item | S | ✅ | 2026-05-10. | **`appkit/src/next/routing/route-map.ts`**: add `WHATSAPP: "/store/whatsapp"` to `DEFAULT_ROUTE_MAP.STORE`. **`src/constants/navigation.tsx`**: add `{ href: String(ROUTES.STORE.WHATSAPP), label: "WhatsApp" }` to `STORE_NAV_GROUPS` "Store" group after COUPONS. |

---

## Tier GD — In-App Guide Pages *(low priority — post-alpha)*

> **Design intent**: Rich, section-based guide pages embedded in all three dashboards (admin, store, buyer) and the public help center. Unlike the FAQ system (short Q&A answers), guides are long-form reference documents with step-by-step walkthroughs, field-by-field form explanations, status lifecycle diagrams, capability/permission upgrade prompts, and plain-language summaries written for non-technical users. Goal: any user — seller, buyer, or internal employee — should be able to understand every feature, form, and workflow without leaving the app.
>
> **Three guide surfaces**: (1) **Admin guide** — lives at `/admin/guide/*`, accessible to all admin and employee roles; permission-aware (only shows sections the logged-in employee can access). Covers every admin panel and all 18 employee permission groups. (2) **Store guide** — lives inside `/store/guide/*`, accessible only to store owners. Covers every seller-facing feature and all 18 store capabilities. (3) **Buyer help center** — lives at public `/help/*`, accessible without login. Covers the complete buyer journey.
>
> **Sidebar placement (enforced for all three)**: every guide hub must have a dedicated nav entry in its dashboard sidebar — admin: `ADMIN_NAV_GROUPS` Help group (bottom of sidebar); store: `STORE_NAV_GROUPS` Help group; user dashboard: `USER_NAV_GROUPS` Help link pointing to public `/help`. Sidebar entries are wired in GD13 for admin; GD1 already covers store; GD7 covers the user/footer links.
>
> **Content rules**: use only appkit primitives (`Section`, `Container`, `Heading`, `Text`, `Badge`, `Alert`, `Collapsible`, `Stack`, `Row`). No hardcoded hex or breakpoints. All guide content is static (no Firestore reads) — these are pre-authored pages, not CMS-driven. Brand name **LetItRip** throughout. Collectibles-niche examples only (Pokémon TCG, Hot Wheels, Beyblades, anime figures).
>
> **Sequence**: GD1–GD6 (store guides) and GD7–GD11 (buyer guides) are independent. GD12 depends on RBAC8. GD13–GD22 (admin guides) depend on RBAC1 for permission-aware rendering but can be built as static pages first and made permission-aware in the same session as RBAC3/RBAC7.

Requires `admin:stores:read` or full admin. **Section 1 — Store lifecycle**: how stores are created (seller registers → creates store via onboarding → admin reviews); store status values (`active` / `suspended` / `pending_review`); `isVerified` badge — what it means and requirements. **Section 2 — Store identity architecture** (critical rule): `storeId = storeSlug` (public-facing, used in all product/order references); `ownerId = Firebase Auth UID` (internal only — never exposed in API responses); why these are separate (allows future store ownership transfer); the two-step lookup pattern (never join by ownerId in public queries). **Section 3 — Store editor walkthrough**: every field in AdminStoreEditorView — storeName, storeDescription, ownerId (read-only after creation), status Select, isVerified toggle, shippingConfig, payoutDetails (UPI + bank — treated as PII); how to update payoutDetails safely (masked in UI, encrypted in Firestore). **Section 4 — Capabilities management**: the 18 `StoreCapability` flags explained (see GD5 for the full table); how to grant/revoke via AdminStoreEditorView Capabilities section (RBAC8); which capabilities require contractual paperwork before granting (`lower_commission_rate`, `extended_return_window`, `api_access`). **Section 5 — Store addresses (pickup locations)**: `storeAddresses` collection — `storeId` must match the store slug exactly; `isPickupLocation` flag; max pickup locations per store (no hard limit, but admin convention is ≤3); `storeId` MUST use `store-` prefix (SL6 constraint). **Section 6 — Suspending a store**: what `status: "suspended"` does (hides all products from search; store profile shows "Unavailable" banner; seller receives notification); vs hard-banning the owner user (which cascades to suspend the store — GD22 covers this). `npx tsc --noEmit` → 0 errors. |
| GD17 | Admin: Orders, Returns & Finance Guide | M | ⏳ | **New page** `/admin/guide/orders`. **New view** `AdminOrdersGuideView`. Requires `admin:orders:read` or full admin. **Section 1 — Order statuses**: all 7 statuses (PENDING / PROCESSING / SHIPPED / DELIVERED / CANCELLED / REFUNDED / RETURN_REQUESTED) — who can transition each (buyer, seller, admin, system); admin-only transitions (force-cancel, force-refund). **Section 2 — Order ID format**: `order-{itemCount}-{YYYYMMDD}-{rand6}` — why itemCount is in the ID (quick triage for complex orders); how to search by order ID in the admin panel. **Section 3 — Intervening in a dispute**: when admin steps in (seller unresponsive for 3 days on return; buyer escalation via support ticket); admin dispute tools (force-accept return, issue platform credit — future). **Section 4 — Payouts**: payout cycle (weekly); payout status (PENDING → PROCESSING → PAID / FAILED); what to do on FAILED payout (check store payoutDetails — UPI/bank details may be stale; contact seller via store email); `ordersIncluded` array — which delivered orders are bundled in each payout batch. **Section 5 — Return requests**: admin visibility into return reason + photos; when to override seller reject (if evidence clearly supports buyer's claim); refund timeline after admin override. **Section 6 — Commission & settlement math**: how `siteSettings.fees.platformFee` is applied; what `customCommissionRate` means (for `lower_commission_rate` capability stores — stored on `StoreDocument`); how to audit a payout batch calculation. **Section 7 — Auction settlement**: what happens when an auction ends with no payment (auto-cancel → system notify next bidder); admin manual override if system fails. `npx tsc --noEmit` → 0 errors. |
| GD18 | Admin: Content & Marketing Guide | M | ⏳ | **New page** `/admin/guide/content`. **New view** `AdminContentGuideView`. Requires any content permission or full admin. **Section 1 — Blog posts**: post statuses (draft / published); `readTimeMinutes` auto-calculated from content length (or manual override); `youtubeId` for embedded videos; `isFeaured` vs `isFeatured` on homepage section — difference (featured flag drives section query, not the homepage section config directly); rich text content rules (no raw Firebase Storage URLs in body — always `/api/media/` proxy). **Section 2 — Events**: event types (TOURNAMENT / CONVENTION / MEETUP / SALE); event statuses driven by `startsAt`/`endsAt` (upcoming → active → ended — system-computed, not manually set); `eventEntries` subcollection — CONFIRMED / WAITLISTED / CANCELLED states; `stats.totalEntries` vs `stats.approvedEntries` (total = submitted, approved = CONFIRMED); when to manually cancel an entry vs soft-ban the user from joining events. **Section 3 — FAQs**: category values and which pages they appear on (`showOnHomepage`, `showInFooter`); `searchTokens[]` array — must be manually filled (drives FAQ search); `priority` + `order` — priority is used for sorting within category, `order` is global absolute position; `isPinned` shows FAQ above non-pinned in its category. **Section 4 — Carousel slides**: MAX_ACTIVE_SLIDES = 5; `background.type` (image/video/color/gradient); `cards[]` array inside each slide; how to reorder slides (drag in AdminCarouselView); why you cannot have 2 slides of the same `background.type: "video"` active at once (performance constraint). **Section 5 — Homepage sections**: 21 section types; `order` field drives render sequence; `enabled: false` hides without deleting; config shape varies per type — always refer to `appkit/src/features/homepage/schemas/firestore.ts` for the authoritative shape; never manually edit Firestore documents — always use AdminSectionsView. **Section 6 — Ads**: ad slot keys and where they render on the page; `isActive` vs `startDate`/`endDate` scheduling; `impressions` + `clicks` counters are read-only. **Section 7 — Newsletter**: how subscribers are stored; export flow; legal note (CAN-SPAM / Indian IT Act — unsubscribe must be honoured). `npx tsc --noEmit` → 0 errors. |
| GD19 | Admin: Site Configuration Guide | S | ⏳ | **New page** `/admin/guide/site`. **New view** `AdminSiteConfigGuideView`. Requires `admin:site:read` or full admin. **Section 1 — Site Settings overview**: the 12 setting groups (branding, appearance, announcementBanner, seoDefaults, contactSocial, watermark, fees, integrations, shipping, auctionConfig, platformLimits, legalPages); singleton document at `site_settings/global` — only one exists; never delete this document. **Section 2 — Integrations (API keys)**: which keys are stored here (Razorpay, Firebase, Shiprocket, WhatsApp, SendGrid, Google Analytics, etc.); keys are write-only in the UI (shown as "••••••" after saving); how to rotate a key (enter new value, save — old value is immediately replaced); warn: deleting the value from the UI does NOT rotate the key at the provider — revoke it there first. **Section 3 — Platform limits**: `maxOpenTicketsPerUser` (default 2); `maxOrderTicketsPerOrder` (default 1); `maxImagesPerProduct`; `minBidIncrementPaise`; `auctionConfig.defaultExtensionMinutes`; `auctionConfig.paymentWindowHours` — changing these mid-operation affects all in-flight auctions and tickets, so change with care. **Section 4 — Navigation editor**: `nav-` prefix for nav items; adding a nav item to `MAIN_NAV_ITEMS` in admin makes it appear in the public top bar; `isExternal: true` for external links (opens in new tab); never delete a nav item that is referenced in marketing materials without replacing the URL. **Section 5 — Feature flags**: what feature flags control (experimental features, A/B tests); how to roll out (set flag → test in staging → set for all). `npx tsc --noEmit` → 0 errors. |
| GD20 | Admin: Team & Permissions Guide — employee onboarding reference | L | ⏳ | **New page** `/admin/guide/team`. **New view** `AdminTeamGuideView`. Requires `admin:team:read` or full admin. **Section 1 — Employee vs admin**: `role: "admin"` bypasses ALL permission checks; `role: "employee"` can only access sections granted by `permissions[]`; why admin access should be minimised (audit trail, least privilege); the Firebase Auth `admin: true` custom claim and how it maps to Firestore rules (RBAC9). **Section 2 — Permission groups table** (the main reference for this guide): full table of all 18 preset `EmployeeGroup` values — one row per group with: group name, typical job title, exact permissions list (pulled from `PERMISSION_GROUPS` constant — rendered as readable chips not raw strings). Groups: `content_moderator` (moderates reviews + comments), `review_manager` (reviews + products:read), `blog_poster` (blog:read/write/publish), `community_manager` (events + newsletter + contact), `event_handler` (events read/write/delete + entries), `newsletter_manager` (newsletter + contact), `seo_manager` (site:read + faqs + blog:read + analytics:view), `ad_manager` (ads + featured + deals), `site_manager` (site:read/write + navigation + sections + carousel + ads + feature-flags), `catalog_manager` (products + categories + brands + reviews:read + media), `finance_manager` (payouts + orders:read + analytics:view), `data_analyst` (analytics:view + orders:read + users:read + carts:read + wishlists:read), `customer_support` (support-tickets:read/write/assign/close + orders:read/write + returns:read/write + users:read + contact:read + notifications:read/write), `store_onboarding` (stores:read/write + store-addresses:read + brands:read + categories:read + users:read), `trust_and_safety` (user-bans:read/write + support-tickets all + scammers:read/write/verify + users:read + media:read/write), `auction_monitor` (bids:read/write + products:read + orders:read + users:read), `scam_moderator` (scammers:read/write/verify/delete + users:read + media:read/write), `support_agent` (dashboard:view + support-tickets:read/write/assign/close + orders:read/write + returns:read/write + users:read + contact:read + notifications:read/write). **Section 3 — Inviting an employee**: step-by-step (Admin Team page → Invite Employee → enter email + select group → system sends invite email with temp password → employee logs in → forced password change). **Section 4 — Customising permissions** ("Custom" group): when to deviate from a preset; the domain tabs in the editor (Management / Finance / Catalog / Content / Site / Events); System tab intentionally omitted from employee permission picker (sessions, feature-flags, copilot, team are admin-only). **Section 5 — Revoking access**: what "Revoke access" does (sets `isDisabled: true` + clears `permissions` — does NOT delete user doc for audit trail); why revoking is preferable to deleting; how to re-enable (set `isDisabled: false` + re-assign permissions). **Section 6 — Permission audit best practices**: review employee permissions quarterly; log of who granted what is stored in `users/{uid}/banHistory` subcollection (reused for permission change events). `npx tsc --noEmit` → 0 errors. |
| GD21 | Admin: Analytics Guide | S | ⏳ | **New page** `/admin/guide/analytics`. **New view** `AdminAnalyticsGuideView`. Requires `admin:analytics:view` or full admin. **Section 1 — What analytics show**: current analytics dashboard metrics (orders, GMV, user signups, active auctions, product views — all from Firestore aggregates or live-stats queries); what is NOT tracked (individual user browsing sessions — no GA-style clickstream). **Section 2 — Live stats vs seed stats**: live metrics query Firestore in real time; seed data populates `stats.*` denormalized fields on user/store/product documents — these are eventually consistent (updated by Cloud Functions on write events, not on read). **Section 3 — Payout analytics**: how to interpret payout batch reports; PAID vs PENDING amounts; how to cross-reference with orders. **Section 4 — Store performance** (for `data_analyst` and `finance_manager`): store-level order counts, GMV, avg rating — these are denormalized on `StoreDocument.stats`; when stats fall out of sync (Cloud Function lag) and how to trigger a manual recalculation (future admin action). **Section 5 — Advanced analytics** (for stores with `advanced_analytics` capability): cohort retention, basket analysis, top-buyer breakdown — these require Firestore aggregation queries and are only available to capability-enabled stores + admin. **Section 6 — Data export** (future): CSV export flow (future VA19 task); PII handling rules for exports (email/phone must be HMAC-de-identified before export to non-admin staff). `npx tsc --noEmit` → 0 errors. |
| GD22 | Admin: Trust & Safety Guide — bans, scams, support tickets | L | ⏳ | **New page** `/admin/guide/trust`. **New view** `AdminTrustGuideView`. Requires `admin:user-bans:read` or `admin:scammers:read` or `admin:support-tickets:read` or full admin — show only the sections the employee has access to. **Section 1 — Soft bans vs hard bans**: soft ban = restricts specific actions (`BannedAction` values: `write_reviews`, `write_blog_comments`, `join_events`, `place_bids`, `create_listings`, `send_messages`, `create_support_tickets`, `report_scammers`) while account remains active; hard ban = disables Firebase Auth account, suspends store, cancels bids, revokes sessions — nuclear option; when to use each (soft ban: single policy violation; hard ban: fraud, persistent abuse, legal requirement). **Section 2 — Applying a soft ban** (step-by-step): open Admin Users → find user → Moderation tab → Add soft ban → select action + reason + optional expiry → Save; user receives notification immediately; ban is enforced server-side on the relevant API route; expired bans are treated as lifted without deletion. **Section 3 — Applying a hard ban** (step-by-step + cascade effects): Moderation tab → "Suspend account" toggle → enter reason → Confirm; cascade: Auth disabled → sessions deleted → store suspended → active bids cancelled → notification sent to user; how to lift (Unban button — does NOT auto-restore listings). **Section 4 — Ban appeal process**: user contacts support via email (not ticket — `create_support_tickets` is soft-banned); `trust_and_safety` employee reviews evidence; lift via Admin Users → Moderation tab. **Section 5 — Scam report workflow** (for `scam_moderator` and `trust_and_safety`): report comes in with `status: "pending_review"`; admin reviews identity + evidence + incident description; "Verify & Publish" (sets `status: "verified"`, notifies reporter) vs "Reject" (notifies reporter with reason); editing a verified profile (updating fields does NOT reset status); contest handling — if accused contests, review `contests` subcollection → "Uphold" (update profile + mark contest resolved) vs "Dismiss"; when to "Remove" a verified profile (false identity, legal takedown). **Section 6 — Support ticket workflow** (for `customer_support` and `support_agent`): ticket states (open → in_progress → waiting_on_user → resolved → closed); who can do what (read: all support roles; write/reply: read/write; assign: assign permission; close: close permission); SLA guidelines (first response within 4 hours for high/urgent; 24 hours for normal; 48 hours for low); escalation path (escalate priority + notify all `admin:support-tickets:read` employees); internal notes field (never visible to user — use for escalation context, account observations). **Section 7 — Trust metrics** (`Alert variant="info"`): how `helpfulCount` on reviews works; how `views` on scammer profiles is used (trending scam types); how to interpret `reportedByAnon` (reporter chose anonymity — do not expose their identity even internally). `npx tsc --noEmit` → 0 errors. |

| SB4-H | Prize Reveal API route — crypto.randomInt + pool exhaustion | M | ⏳ | **New file:** `src/app/api/prize-draws/[id]/reveal/route.ts`. POST `{ orderId }`. Auth required. Steps: verify order ownership + paid; verify `order.prizeDrawProductId === productId`; idempotency check (`order.prizeWon === null`); verify `prizeRevealStatus === "open"` + within window + before deadline; filter `unwonItems`; if empty → refund + return `{ refunded: true, reason: "pool_exhausted" }`; else `crypto.randomInt(0, unwonItems.length)` → pick winner; update order.prizeWon; set prizeDrawItem.isWon=true; return `{ prizeWon: { itemNumber, title, images, estimatedValue } }`. `npx tsc --noEmit` → 0 errors. |
| SB4-I | PrizeRevealModal component | M | ⏳ | **New file:** `appkit/src/features/products/components/PrizeRevealModal.tsx`. Triggered on order detail page when reveal conditions met. Countdown to deadline. "Reveal My Prize" button → API call. CSS card-flip animation on success. Shows won item: number, title, images, estimated value, RNG Source Code link. If already revealed: show won item directly without re-draw. `npx tsc --noEmit` → 0 errors. |

### SB11 — Homepage Sections: Bundles, Prize Draws & Event Raffles

> **Why here:** Bundles and prize draws are new listing types (SB1–SB4). They need dedicated homepage section types so the CMS admin can surface them on the homepage — the same way standard products, auctions, and pre-orders already have section types. Event raffles (SB9) also get a section type so live raffle events can be promoted on the homepage. All three section types are **additive** — no existing section types change. Seed docs are disabled-by-default so they don't render before the underlying data exists. SB11 depends on the schemas from SB1-A (listingType), SB1-E (BundleDocument), SB4 (PrizeDrawDocument shape), and SB9-A/SB9-B (EventType raffle). SB11 can be planned and scaffolded independently; it needs SB3/SB4/SB9 data to actually render anything.
>
> **Relationship to SB5-D:** SB5-D planned seeding `section-featured-bundles` and `section-prize-draws` as "reuse existing section types". Those types don't exist yet. SB11-A defines them. SB11-G handles the three new disabled seed docs. SB5-D should be updated to only seed `section-brand-hot-wheels` and `section-brand-pokemon` (which reuse existing `brand-spotlight` or `brands` section types).
>
> **Session assignment:** SB11 fits into Session 93 alongside EX1–EX5/YT1 (extended homepage sections). All three new section components are async RSC and query their own collections — no architecture change needed.

| # | Task | Complexity | Status | Notes |
|---|------|-----------|--------|-------|
| SB11-A | Schema — 3 new HomepageSectionType values + config interfaces | M | ⏳ | **File:** `appkit/src/features/homepage/schemas/firestore.ts`. Add `"featured-bundles" \| "prize-draws" \| "event-raffles"` to `HomepageSectionType` union. Add config interfaces: **`FeaturedBundlesSectionConfig`** `{ title?: string; subtitle?: string; maxItems?: number; storeId?: string; categorySlug?: string; sortBy?: "newest" \| "savings-desc" \| "price-asc"; showSavingsBadge?: boolean }`. **`PrizeDrawsSectionConfig`** `{ title?: string; subtitle?: string; maxItems?: number; storeId?: string; revealStatus?: "pending" \| "open" \| "all"; showCountdown?: boolean; showEntriesRemaining?: boolean }`. **`EventRafflesSectionConfig`** `{ title?: string; subtitle?: string; maxItems?: number; raffleType?: "raffle" \| "spin_wheel" \| "all"; showEntryCount?: boolean; showCountdown?: boolean }`. Add to `HomepageSectionConfig` discriminated union. Update exhaustive switch in any type narrower. `npx tsc --noEmit` → 0 errors. |

Add Firestore composite indexes required: `bundles: status+createdAt`, `bundles: status+storeId+createdAt`, `bundles: status+categorySlug+createdAt`, `events: hasRaffle+status+startsAt`. Add to `appkit/firebase/base/firestore.indexes.json`. `npx tsc --noEmit` → 0 errors. |
| SB11-G | Seed — 3 disabled homepage section docs | S | ⏳ | **File:** `appkit/src/seed/homepage-sections-seed-data.ts`. Add (all `enabled: false` — no data yet): `section-featured-bundles` (type: `"featured-bundles"`, order: 20, config: `{ title: "Curated Bundles", subtitle: "Everything you need in one deal", maxItems: 8, sortBy: "savings-desc", showSavingsBadge: true }`). `section-prize-draws` (type: `"prize-draws"`, order: 21, config: `{ title: "Prize Draws", subtitle: "Enter for a chance to win rare collectibles", maxItems: 6, showCountdown: true, showEntriesRemaining: true, revealStatus: "all" }`). `section-event-raffles` (type: `"event-raffles"`, order: 22, config: `{ title: "Live Raffles & Spin Wheels", subtitle: "Participate in community events and win prizes", maxItems: 4, raffleType: "all", showEntryCount: true, showCountdown: true }`). Update SeedPanel `FieldDef[]` for `homepageSections` to note these 3 new types. `npx tsc --noEmit` → 0 errors. |
